## [1. Awesome Cheminformatics](/content/hsiaoyi0504/awesome-cheminformatics/week/README.md)

### Libraries / General Purpose

*   [CGRtools (‚≠ê26)](https://github.com/cimm-kzn/CGRtools) - Toolkit for processing molecules, reactions and condensed graphs of reactions. Can be used for chemical standardization, MCS search, tautomers generation with backward compatibility to RDKit and NetworkX.

## [4. Awesome Bitcoin Payment Processors](/content/alexk111/awesome-bitcoin-payment-processors/week/README.md)

### Self-Hosted Bitcoin Payment Processors

- Processor: [SatSale (‚≠ê151)](https://github.com/nickfarrow/SatSale)

  Fees: No fees

  Lightning: Yes

  Directly to Your Wallet: Yes

  Conversion to Fiat: Weakhands: [swap to USDT on Liquid (‚≠ê151)](https://github.com/nickfarrow/SatSale/blob/master/config.toml#L82), no-KYC

  Requirements: A Bitcoin node and Python. Lightning node & Woocommerce optional

## [8. Awesome Cybersecurity Blueteam](/content/fabacab/awesome-cybersecurity-blueteam/week/README.md)

### Transport-layer defenses / Overlay and Virtual Private Networks (VPNs)

*   [IPsec VPN Server Auto Setup Scripts (‚≠ê21k)](https://github.com/hwdsl2/setup-ipsec-vpn) - Scripts to build your own IPsec VPN server, with IPsec/L2TP, Cisco IPsec and IKEv2.
*   [Innernet (‚≠ê4.1k)](https://github.com/tonarino/innernet) - Free Software private network system that uses WireGuard under the hood, made to be self-hosted.
*   [Nebula (‚≠ê11k)](https://github.com/slackhq/nebula) - Completely open source and self-hosted, scalable overlay networking tool with a focus on performance, simplicity, and security, inspired by tinc.
*   [OpenVPN](https://openvpn.net/) - Longstanding Free Software traditional SSL/TLS-based virtual private network.
*   [Tailscale](https://tailscale.com/) - Managed freemium mesh VPN service built on top of WireGuard.
*   [tinc](https://tinc-vpn.org/) - Free Software mesh VPN implemented entirely in userspace that supports expandable network space, bridged ethernet segments, and more.

## [10. Awesome Go](/content/avelino/awesome-go/week/README.md)

### Audio and Music

*   [flac (‚≠ê242)](https://github.com/mewkiz/flac) - Native Go FLAC encoder/decoder with support for FLAC streams.
*   [gaad (‚≠ê110)](https://github.com/Comcast/gaad) - Native Go AAC bitstream parser.
*   [GoAudio (‚≠ê278)](https://github.com/DylanMeeus/GoAudio) - Native Go Audio Processing Library.
*   [gosamplerate (‚≠ê27)](https://github.com/dh1tw/gosamplerate) - libsamplerate bindings for go.
*   [id3v2 (‚≠ê283)](https://github.com/bogem/id3v2) - ID3 decoding and encoding library for Go.
*   [malgo (‚≠ê216)](https://github.com/gen2brain/malgo) - Mini audio library.
*   [minimp3 (‚≠ê99)](https://github.com/tosone/minimp3) - Lightweight MP3 decoder library.
*   [Oto (‚≠ê1.2k)](https://github.com/hajimehoshi/oto) - A low-level library to play sound on multiple platforms.
*   [PortAudio (‚≠ê574)](https://github.com/gordonklaus/portaudio) - Go bindings for the PortAudio audio I/O library.

### Authentication and OAuth

*   [branca (‚≠ê50)](https://github.com/essentialkaos/branca) - branca token [specification implementation (‚≠ê199)](https://github.com/tuupola/branca-spec) for Golang 1.15+.
*   [go-jose (‚≠ê2k)](https://github.com/square/go-jose) - Fairly complete implementation of the JOSE working group's JSON Web Token, JSON Web Signatures, and JSON Web Encryption specs.
*   [gologin (‚≠ê1.6k)](https://github.com/dghubble/gologin) - chainable handlers for login with OAuth1 and OAuth2 authentication providers.
*   [gorbac (‚≠ê1.4k)](https://github.com/mikespook/gorbac) - provides a lightweight role-based access control (RBAC) implementation in Golang.
*   [goth (‚≠ê4k)](https://github.com/markbates/goth) - provides a simple, clean, and idiomatic way to use OAuth and OAuth2. Handles multiple providers out of the box.
*   [jwt (‚≠ê308)](https://github.com/pascaldekloe/jwt) - Lightweight JSON Web Token (JWT) library.
*   [jwt-auth (‚≠ê226)](https://github.com/adam-hanna/jwt-auth) - JWT middleware for Golang http servers with many configuration options.
*   [loginsrv (‚≠ê1.9k)](https://github.com/tarent/loginsrv) - JWT login microservice with plugable backends such as OAuth2 (Github), htpasswd, osiam.
*   [osin (‚≠ê1.8k)](https://github.com/openshift/osin) - Golang OAuth2 server library.
*   [otpgen (‚≠ê122)](https://github.com/grijul/otpgen) - Library to generate TOTP/HOTP codes.
*   [otpgo (‚≠ê53)](https://github.com/jltorresm/otpgo) - Time-Based One-Time Password (TOTP) and HMAC-Based One-Time Password (HOTP) library for Go.
*   [paseto (‚≠ê680)](https://github.com/o1egl/paseto) - Golang implementation of Platform-Agnostic Security Tokens (PASETO).
*   [scope (‚≠ê29)](https://github.com/SonicRoshan/scope) - Easily Manage OAuth2 Scopes In Go.
*   [scs (‚≠ê1.4k)](https://github.com/alexedwards/scs) - Session Manager for HTTP servers.
*   [securecookie (‚≠ê67)](https://github.com/chmike/securecookie) - Efficient secure cookie encoding/decoding.
*   [session (‚≠ê111)](https://github.com/icza/session) - Go session management for web servers (including support for Google App Engine - GAE).
*   [sessions (‚≠ê72)](https://github.com/adam-hanna/sessions) - Dead simple, highly performant, highly customizable sessions service for go http servers.
*   [sessionup (‚≠ê119)](https://github.com/swithek/sessionup) - Simple, yet effective HTTP session management and identification package.
*   [sjwt (‚≠ê110)](https://github.com/brianvoe/sjwt) - Simple jwt generator and parser.

### Blockchain

*   [cosmos-sdk (‚≠ê5k)](https://github.com/cosmos/cosmos-sdk) - A Framework for Building Public Blockchains in the Cosmos Ecosystem.
*   [go-ethereum (‚≠ê41k)](https://github.com/ethereum/go-ethereum) - Official Go implementation of the Ethereum protocol.
*   [gossamer (‚≠ê375)](https://github.com/ChainSafe/gossamer) - A Go implementation of the Polkadot Host.
*   [solana-go (‚≠ê408)](https://github.com/gagliardetto/solana-go) - Go library to interface with Solana JSON RPC and WebSocket interfaces.
*   [tendermint (‚≠ê5.4k)](https://github.com/tendermint/tendermint) - High-performance middleware for transforming a state machine written in any programming language into a Byzantine Fault Tolerant replicated state machine using the Tendermint consensus and blockchain protocols.

*   [larry (‚≠ê120)](https://github.com/ezeoleaf/larry) - Larry üê¶ is a really simple Twitter bot generator that tweets random repositories from Github built in Go.

*   [slack-bot (‚≠ê133)](https://github.com/innogames/slack-bot) - Ready to use Slack Bot for lazy developers: Custom commands, Jenkins, Jira, Bitbucket, Github...

### Advanced Console UIs

*   [asciigraph (‚≠ê2.2k)](https://github.com/guptarohit/asciigraph) - Go package to make lightweight ASCII line graph ‚ï≠‚îà‚ïØ in command line apps with no other dependencies.

*   [gookit/color (‚≠ê1.3k)](https://github.com/gookit/color) - Terminal color rendering tool library, support 16 colors, 256 colors, RGB color rendering output, compatible with Windows.

*   [progressbar (‚≠ê3.1k)](https://github.com/schollz/progressbar) - Basic thread-safe progress bar that works in every OS.
*   [pterm (‚≠ê3.3k)](https://github.com/pterm/pterm) - A library to beautify console output on every platform with many combinable components.
*   [spinner (‚≠ê2k)](https://github.com/briandowns/spinner) - Go package to easily provide a terminal spinner with options.

*   [termenv (‚≠ê1.3k)](https://github.com/muesli/termenv) - Advanced ANSI style & color support for your terminal applications.
*   [termui (‚≠ê12k)](https://github.com/gizak/termui) - Go terminal dashboard based on **termbox-go** and inspired by [blessed-contrib (‚≠ê15k)](https://github.com/yaronn/blessed-contrib).

### Standard CLI

*   [argparse (‚≠ê504)](https://github.com/akamensky/argparse) - Command line argument parser inspired by Python's argparse module.
*   [argv (‚≠ê37)](https://github.com/cosiner/argv) - Go library to split command line string as arguments array using the bash syntax.

*   [carapace-bin (‚≠ê174)](https://github.com/rsteube/carapace-bin) - Multi-shell multi-command argument completer.
*   [cli (‚≠ê680)](https://github.com/mkideal/cli) - Feature-rich and easy to use command-line package based on golang struct tags.
*   [cli (‚≠ê119)](https://github.com/teris-io/cli) - Simple and complete API for building command line interfaces in Go.
*   [climax (‚≠ê206)](https://github.com/tucnak/climax) - Alternative CLI with "human face", in spirit of Go command.
*   [cl√Ær (‚≠ê152)](https://github.com/leaanthony/clir) - A Simple and Clear CLI library. Dependency free.
*   [cmd (‚≠ê35)](https://github.com/posener/cmd) - Extends the standard `flag` package to support sub commands and more in idiomatic way.
*   [cmdr (‚≠ê120)](https://github.com/hedzr/cmdr) - A POSIX/GNU style, getopt-like command-line UI Go library.

*   [complete (‚≠ê878)](https://github.com/posener/complete) - Write bash completions in Go + Go command bash completion.
*   [Dnote (‚≠ê2.5k)](https://github.com/dnote/dnote) - A simple command line notebook with multi-device sync.

*   [env (‚≠ê103)](https://github.com/codingconcepts/env) - Tag-based environment configuration for structs.
*   [flag (‚≠ê123)](https://github.com/cosiner/flag) - Simple but powerful command line option parsing library for Go supporting subcommand.
*   [flaggy (‚≠ê821)](https://github.com/integrii/flaggy) - A robust and idiomatic flags package with excellent subcommand support.
*   [flagvar (‚≠ê41)](https://github.com/sgreben/flagvar) - A collection of flag argument types for Go's standard `flag` package.

*   [job (‚≠ê124)](https://github.com/liujianping/job) - JOB, make your short-term command as a long-term job.
*   [kingpin (‚≠ê3.3k)](https://github.com/alecthomas/kingpin) - Command line and flag parser supporting sub commands (superseded by `kong`; see below).

*   [ts (‚≠ê16)](https://github.com/liujianping/ts) - Timestamp convert & compare tool.

### Configuration

*   [aconfig (‚≠ê428)](https://github.com/cristalhq/aconfig) - Simple, useful and opinionated config loader.
*   [cleanenv (‚≠ê920)](https://github.com/ilyakaznacheev/cleanenv) - Minimalistic configuration reader (from files, ENV, and wherever you want).
*   [config (‚≠ê322)](https://github.com/JeremyLoy/config) - Cloud native application configuration. Bind ENV to structs in only two lines.
*   [config (‚≠ê261)](https://github.com/olebedev/config) - JSON or YAML configuration wrapper with environment variables and flags parsing.
*   [configuration (‚≠ê81)](https://github.com/BoRuDar/configuration) - Library for initializing configuration structs from env variables, files, flags and 'default' tag.
*   [configure (‚≠ê57)](https://github.com/paked/configure) - Provides configuration through multiple sources, including JSON, flags and environment variables.
*   [configuro (‚≠ê87)](https://github.com/sherifabdlnaby/configuro) - opinionated configuration loading & validation framework from ENV and Files focused towards 12-Factor compliant applications.
*   [confita (‚≠ê458)](https://github.com/heetch/confita) - Load configuration in cascade from multiple backends into a struct.
*   [conflate (‚≠ê27)](https://github.com/the4thamigo-uk/conflate) - Library/tool to merge multiple JSON/YAML/TOML files from arbitrary URLs, validation against a JSON schema, and application of default values defined in the schema.
*   [env (‚≠ê3.3k)](https://github.com/caarlos0/env) - Parse environment variables to Go structs (with defaults).
*   [env (‚≠ê39)](https://github.com/junk1tm/env) - A lightweight package for loading environment variables into structs.
*   [envcfg (‚≠ê99)](https://github.com/tomazk/envcfg) - Un-marshaling environment variables to Go structs.
*   [envconf (‚≠ê11)](https://github.com/ian-kent/envconf) - Configuration from environment.
*   [envconfig (‚≠ê234)](https://github.com/vrischmann/envconfig) - Read your configuration from environment variables.
*   [envh (‚≠ê96)](https://github.com/antham/envh) - Helpers to manage environment variables.
*   [fig (‚≠ê255)](https://github.com/kkyr/fig) - Tiny library for reading configuration from a file and from environment variables (with validation & defaults).
*   [gcfg (‚≠ê162)](https://github.com/go-gcfg/gcfg) - read INI-style configuration files into Go structs; supports user-defined types and subsections.
*   [genv (‚≠ê31)](https://github.com/sakirsensoy/genv) - Read environment variables easily with dotenv support.
*   [go-aws-ssm (‚≠ê54)](https://github.com/PaddleHQ/go-aws-ssm) - Go package that fetches parameters from AWS System Manager - Parameter Store.
*   [go-conf (‚≠ê6)](https://github.com/ThomasObenaus/go-conf) - Simple library for application configuration based on annotated structs. It supports reading the configuration from environment variables, config files and command line parameters.
*   [go-ini (‚≠ê9)](https://github.com/subpop/go-ini) - A Go package that marshals and unmarshals INI-files.
*   [go-ssm-config (‚≠ê17)](https://github.com/ianlopshire/go-ssm-config) - Go utility for loading configuration parameters from AWS SSM (Parameter Store).
*   [go-up (‚≠ê39)](https://github.com/ufoscout/go-up) - A simple configuration library with recursive placeholders resolution and no magic.
*   [goConfig (‚≠ê3)](https://github.com/crgimenes/goConfig) - Parses a struct as input and populates the fields of this struct with parameters from command line, environment variables and configuration file.
*   [godotenv (‚≠ê5.9k)](https://github.com/joho/godotenv) - Go port of Ruby's dotenv library (Loads environment variables from `.env`).
*   [gofigure (‚≠ê65)](https://github.com/ian-kent/gofigure) - Go application configuration made easy.
*   [gone/jconf (‚≠ê45)](https://github.com/One-com/gone/tree/master/jconf) - Modular JSON configuration. Keep you config structs along with the code they configure and delegate parsing to submodules without sacrificing full config serialization.
*   [gonfig (‚≠ê6)](https://github.com/milad-abbasi/gonfig) - Tag-based configuration parser which loads values from different providers into typesafe struct.
*   [gookit/config (‚≠ê442)](https://github.com/gookit/config) - application config manage(load,get,set). support JSON, YAML, TOML, INI, HCL. multi file load, data override merge.
*   [hjson (‚≠ê293)](https://github.com/hjson/hjson-go) - Human JSON, a configuration file format for humans. Relaxed syntax, fewer mistakes, more comments.
*   [hocon (‚≠ê56)](https://github.com/gurkankaymak/hocon) - Configuration library for working with the HOCON(a human-friendly JSON superset) format, supports features like environment variables, referencing other values, comments and multiple files.
*   [ingo (‚≠ê35)](https://github.com/schachmat/ingo) - Flags persisted in an ini-like config file.
*   [ini (‚≠ê3.2k)](https://github.com/go-ini/ini) - Go package to read and write INI files.
*   [ini (‚≠ê11)](https://github.com/wlevene/ini) - INI Parser & Write Library, Unmarshal to Struct,Marshal to Json,Write File,watch file.
*   [joshbetz/config (‚≠ê215)](https://github.com/joshbetz/config) - Small configuration library for Go that parses environment variables, JSON files, and reloads automatically on SIGHUP.
*   [kelseyhightower/envconfig (‚≠ê4.4k)](https://github.com/kelseyhightower/envconfig) - Go library for managing configuration data from environment variables.
*   [koanf (‚≠ê1.6k)](https://github.com/knadh/koanf) - Light weight, extensible library for reading config in Go applications. Built in support for JSON, TOML, YAML, env, command line.
*   [konfig (‚≠ê632)](https://github.com/lalamove/konfig) - Composable, observable and performant config handling for Go for the distributed processing era.
*   [mini (‚≠ê34)](https://github.com/sasbury/mini) - Golang package for parsing ini-style configuration files.
*   [nasermirzaei89/env (‚≠ê10)](https://github.com/nasermirzaei89/env) - Simple useful package for read environment variables.
*   [onion (‚≠ê111)](https://github.com/goraz/onion) - Layer based configuration for Go, Supports JSON, TOML, YAML, properties, etcd, env, and encryption using PGP.
*   [piper (‚≠ê7)](https://github.com/Yiling-J/piper) - Viper wrapper with config inheritance and key generation.
*   [store (‚≠ê265)](https://github.com/tucnak/store) - Lightweight configuration manager for Go.
*   [swap (‚≠ê8)](https://github.com/oblq/swap) - Instantiate/configure structs recursively, based on build environment. (YAML, TOML, JSON and env).
*   [typenv (‚≠ê9)](https://github.com/diegomarangoni/typenv) - Minimalistic, zero dependency, typed environment variables library.
*   [uConfig (‚≠ê58)](https://github.com/omeid/uconfig) - Lightweight, zero-dependency, and extendable configuration management.
*   [viper (‚≠ê22k)](https://github.com/spf13/viper) - Go configuration with fangs.
*   [xdg (‚≠ê342)](https://github.com/adrg/xdg) - Go implementation of the [XDG Base Directory Specification](https://specifications.freedesktop.org/basedir-spec/basedir-spec-latest.html) and [XDG user directories](https://wiki.archlinux.org/index.php/XDG_user_directories).
*   [xdg (‚≠ê72)](https://github.com/OpenPeeDeeP/xdg) - Cross platform package that follows the [XDG Standard](https://standards.freedesktop.org/basedir-spec/basedir-spec-latest.html).

### Miscellaneous Data Structures and Algorithms

*   [concurrent-writer (‚≠ê47)](https://github.com/free/concurrent-writer) - Highly concurrent drop-in replacement for `bufio.Writer`.
*   [conjungo (‚≠ê110)](https://github.com/InVisionApp/conjungo) - A small, powerful and flexible merge library.

*   [go-geoindex (‚≠ê344)](https://github.com/hailocab/go-geoindex) - In-memory geo index.

*   [gofal (‚≠ê17)](https://github.com/xxjwxc/gofal) - fractional api for Go.
*   [gota (‚≠ê2.6k)](https://github.com/kniren/gota) - Implementation of dataframes, series, and data wrangling methods for Go.
*   [hide (‚≠ê53)](https://github.com/emvi/hide) - ID type with marshalling to/from hash to prevent sending IDs to clients.
*   [hilbert (‚≠ê259)](https://github.com/google/hilbert) - Go package for mapping values to and from space-filling curves, such as Hilbert and Peano curves.
*   [hyperloglog (‚≠ê831)](https://github.com/axiomhq/hyperloglog) - HyperLogLog implementation with Sparse, LogLog-Beta bias correction and TailCut space reduction.

*   [qry (‚≠ê28)](https://github.com/HnH/qry) - Tool that generates constants from files with raw SQL queries.
*   [sq (‚≠ê188)](https://github.com/bokwoon95/go-structured-query) - Type-safe SQL builder and struct mapper for Go.
*   [sqlf (‚≠ê98)](https://github.com/leporo/sqlf) - Fast SQL query builder.
*   [sqlingo (‚≠ê299)](https://github.com/lqs/sqlingo) - A lightweight DSL to build SQL in Go.
*   [sqrl (‚≠ê250)](https://github.com/elgris/sqrl) - SQL query builder, fork of Squirrel with improved performance.
*   [Squalus](https://gitlab.com/qosenergy/squalus) - Thin layer over the Go SQL package that makes it easier to perform queries.
*   [Squirrel (‚≠ê5.6k)](https://github.com/Masterminds/squirrel) - Go library that helps you build SQL queries.
*   [xo (‚≠ê3.3k)](https://github.com/knq/xo) - Generate idiomatic Go code for databases based on existing schema definitions or custom queries supporting PostgreSQL, MySQL, SQLite, Oracle, and Microsoft SQL Server.

### Date and Time

*   [carbon (‚≠ê3k)](https://github.com/golang-module/carbon) - A simple, semantic and developer-friendly golang package for datetime.
*   [carbon (‚≠ê746)](https://github.com/uniplaces/carbon) - Simple Time extension with a lot of util methods, ported from PHP Carbon library.
*   [cronrange (‚≠ê18)](https://github.com/1set/cronrange) - Parses Cron-style time range expressions, checks if the given time is within any ranges.
*   [date (‚≠ê104)](https://github.com/rickb777/date) - Augments Time for working with dates, date ranges, time spans, periods, and time-of-day.
*   [dateparse (‚≠ê1.8k)](https://github.com/araddon/dateparse) - Parse date's without knowing format in advance.
*   [durafmt (‚≠ê455)](https://github.com/hako/durafmt) - Time duration formatting library for Go.
*   [feiertage (‚≠ê43)](https://github.com/wlbr/feiertage) - Set of functions to calculate public holidays in Germany, incl. specialization on the states of Germany (Bundesl√§nder). Things like Easter, Pentecost, Thanksgiving...
*   [go-persian-calendar (‚≠ê145)](https://github.com/yaa110/go-persian-calendar) - The implementation of the Persian (Solar Hijri) Calendar in Go (golang).
*   [go-str2duration (‚≠ê63)](https://github.com/xhit/go-str2duration) - Convert string to duration. Support time.Duration returned string and more.
*   [go-sunrise (‚≠ê64)](https://github.com/nathan-osman/go-sunrise) - Calculate the sunrise and sunset times for a given location.
*   [go-week (‚≠ê8)](https://github.com/stoewer/go-week) - An efficient package to work with ISO8601 week dates.
*   [gostradamus (‚≠ê177)](https://github.com/bykof/gostradamus) - A Go package for working with dates.
*   [iso8601 (‚≠ê120)](https://github.com/relvacode/iso8601) - Efficiently parse ISO8601 date-times without regex.
*   [kair (‚≠ê25)](https://github.com/GuilhermeCaruso/kair) - Date and Time - Golang Formatting Library.
*   [now (‚≠ê4k)](https://github.com/jinzhu/now) - Now is a time toolkit for golang.
*   [NullTime (‚≠ê13)](https://github.com/kirillDanshin/nulltime) - Nullable `time.Time`.
*   [strftime (‚≠ê12)](https://github.com/awoodbeck/strftime) - C99-compatible strftime formatter.
*   [timespan (‚≠ê82)](https://github.com/SaidinWoT/timespan) - For interacting with intervals of time, defined as a start time and a duration.
*   [timeutil (‚≠ê191)](https://github.com/leekchan/timeutil) - Useful extensions (Timedelta, Strftime, ...) to the golang's time package.
*   [tuesday (‚≠ê12)](https://github.com/osteele/tuesday) - Ruby-compatible Strftime function.

### Distributed Systems

*   [arpc (‚≠ê693)](https://github.com/lesismal/arpc) - More effective network communication, support two-way-calling, notify, broadcast.
*   [celeriac (‚≠ê73)](https://github.com/svcavallar/celeriac.v1) - Library for adding support for interacting and monitoring Celery workers, tasks and events in Go.
*   [consistent (‚≠ê572)](https://github.com/buraksezer/consistent) - Consistent hashing with bounded loads.
*   [consistenthash (‚≠ê16)](https://github.com/mbrostami/consistenthash) - Consistent hashing with configurable replicas.
*   [dht (‚≠ê258)](https://github.com/anacrolix/dht) - BitTorrent Kademlia DHT implementation.

*   [dot (‚≠ê75)](https://github.com/dotchain/dot/) - distributed sync using operational transformation/OT.
*   [doublejump (‚≠ê88)](https://github.com/edwingeng/doublejump) - A revamped Google's jump consistent hash.
*   [dragonboat (‚≠ê4.6k)](https://github.com/lni/dragonboat) - A feature complete and high performance multi-group Raft library in Go.
*   [drmaa (‚≠ê43)](https://github.com/dgruber/drmaa) - Job submission library for cluster schedulers based on the DRMAA standard.
*   [dynamolock](https://cirello.io/dynamolock) - DynamoDB-backed distributed locking implementation.
*   [dynatomic (‚≠ê15)](https://github.com/tylfin/dynatomic) - A library for using DynamoDB as an atomic counter.
*   [emitter-io (‚≠ê3.5k)](https://github.com/emitter-io/emitter) - High performance, distributed, secure and low latency publish-subscribe platform built with MQTT, Websockets and love.
*   [failured (‚≠ê10)](https://github.com/andy2046/failured) - adaptive accrual failure detector for distributed systems.
*   [flowgraph (‚≠ê52)](https://github.com/vectaport/flowgraph) - flow-based programming package.
*   [gleam (‚≠ê3.2k)](https://github.com/chrislusf/gleam) - Fast and scalable distributed map/reduce system written in pure Go and Luajit, combining Go's high concurrency with Luajit's high performance, runs standalone or distributed.
*   [glow (‚≠ê3.1k)](https://github.com/chrislusf/glow) - Easy-to-Use scalable distributed big data processing, Map-Reduce, DAG execution, all in pure Go.
*   [gmsec (‚≠ê22)](https://github.com/gmsec/micro) - A Go distributed systems development framework.
*   [go-doudou (‚≠ê1.1k)](https://github.com/unionj-cloud/go-doudou) - A gossip protocol and OpenAPI 3.0 spec based decentralized microservice framework. Built-in go-doudou cli focusing on low-code and rapid dev can power up your productivity.
*   [go-health (‚≠ê666)](https://github.com/InVisionApp/go-health) - Library for enabling asynchronous dependency health checks in your service.
*   [go-jump (‚≠ê358)](https://github.com/dgryski/go-jump) - Port of Google's "Jump" Consistent Hash function.
*   [go-kit (‚≠ê25k)](https://github.com/go-kit/kit) - Microservice toolkit with support for service discovery, load balancing, pluggable transports, request tracking, etc.

*   [go-mysql-lock (‚≠ê53)](https://github.com/sanketplus/go-mysql-lock) - MySQL based distributed lock.
*   [go-pdu (‚≠ê46)](https://github.com/pdupub/go-pdu) - A decentralized identity-based social network.
*   [go-sundheit (‚≠ê512)](https://github.com/AppsFlyer/go-sundheit) - A library built to provide support for defining async service health checks for golang services.
*   [go-zero (‚≠ê23k)](https://github.com/tal-tech/go-zero) - A web and rpc framework. It's born to ensure the stability of the busy sites with resilient design. Builtin goctl greatly improves the development productivity.
*   [gorpc (‚≠ê674)](https://github.com/valyala/gorpc) - Simple, fast and scalable RPC library for high load.
*   [grpc-go (‚≠ê18k)](https://github.com/grpc/grpc-go) - The Go language implementation of gRPC. HTTP/2 based RPC.

### Error Handling

*   [emperror (‚≠ê288)](https://github.com/emperror/emperror) - Error handling tools and best practices for Go libraries and applications.
*   [eris (‚≠ê1.2k)](https://github.com/rotisserie/eris) - A better way to handle, trace, and log errors in Go. Compatible with the standard error library and github.com/pkg/errors.
*   [errlog (‚≠ê424)](https://github.com/snwfdhmp/errlog) - Hackable package that determines responsible source code for an error (and some other fast-debugging features). Pluggable to any logger in-place.
*   [errors (‚≠ê172)](https://github.com/emperror/errors) - Drop-in replacement for the standard library errors package and github.com/pkg/errors. Provides various error handling primitives.
*   [errors (‚≠ê8k)](https://github.com/pkg/errors) - Package that provides simple error handling primitives.
*   [errors (‚≠ê4)](https://github.com/neuronlabs/errors) - Simple golang error handling with classification primitives.
*   [errors (‚≠ê7)](https://github.com/PumpkinSeed/errors) - The most simple error wrapper with awesome performance and minimal memory overhead.
*   [errorx (‚≠ê954)](https://github.com/joomcode/errorx) - A feature rich error package with stack traces, composition of errors and more.
*   [Falcon (‚≠ê8)](https://github.com/SonicRoshan/falcon) - A Simple Yet Highly Powerful Package For Error Handling.
*   [go-multierror (‚≠ê1.9k)](https://github.com/hashicorp/go-multierror) - Go (golang) package for representing a list of errors as a single error.
*   [tracerr (‚≠ê761)](https://github.com/ztrue/tracerr) - Golang errors with stack trace and source fragments.

*   [bigfile (‚≠ê239)](https://github.com/bigfile/bigfile) - A file transfer system, support to manage files with http api, rpc call and ftp client.
*   [checksum (‚≠ê81)](https://github.com/codingsince1985/checksum) - Compute message digest, like MD5, SHA256, SHA1, CRC or BLAKE2s, for large files.
*   [copy (‚≠ê526)](https://github.com/otiai10/copy) - Copy directory recursively.
*   [flop (‚≠ê33)](https://github.com/homedepot/flop) - File operations library which aims to mirror feature parity with [GNU cp](https://www.gnu.org/software/coreutils/manual/html_node/cp-invocation.html).

*   [go-decent-copy (‚≠ê19)](https://github.com/hugocarreira/go-decent-copy) - Copy files for humans.
*   [go-exiftool (‚≠ê164)](https://github.com/barasher/go-exiftool) - Go bindings for ExifTool, the well-known library used to extract as much metadata as possible (EXIF, IPTC, ...) from files (pictures, PDF, office, ...).
*   [go-gtfs (‚≠ê34)](https://github.com/artonge/go-gtfs) - Load gtfs files in go.
*   [gut/yos (‚≠ê26)](https://github.com/1set/gut) - Simple and reliable package for file operations like copy/move/diff/list on files, directories and symbolic links.
*   [higgs (‚≠ê16)](https://github.com/dastoori/higgs) - A tiny cross-platform Go library to hide/unhide files and directories.
*   [notify (‚≠ê806)](https://github.com/rjeczalik/notify) - File system event notification library with simple API, similar to os/signal.
*   [opc (‚≠ê74)](https://github.com/qmuntal/opc) - Load Open Packaging Conventions (OPC) files for Go.
*   [parquet (‚≠ê62)](https://github.com/parsyl/parquet) - Read and write [parquet](https://parquet.apache.org) files.
*   [pathtype (‚≠ê12)](https://github.com/jonchun/pathtype) - Treat paths as their own type instead of using strings.
*   [pdfcpu (‚≠ê4.6k)](https://github.com/pdfcpu/pdfcpu) - PDF processor.
*   [skywalker (‚≠ê87)](https://github.com/dixonwille/skywalker) - Package to allow one to concurrently go through a filesystem with ease.
*   [tarfs (‚≠ê51)](https://github.com/posener/tarfs) - Implementation of the [`FileSystem` interface](https://godoc.org/github.com/kr/fs#FileSystem) for tar files.
*   [todotxt (‚≠ê18)](https://github.com/1set/todotxt) - Go library for Gina Trapani's [*todo.txt*](http://todotxt.org/) files, supports parsing and manipulating of task lists in the [*todo.txt* format](https://github.com/todotxt/todo.txt).
*   [vfs (‚≠ê217)](https://github.com/C2FO/vfs) - A pluggable, extensible, and opinionated set of filesystem functionality for Go across a number of filesystem types such as os, S3, and GCS.

*   [raylib-go (‚≠ê937)](https://github.com/gen2brain/raylib-go) - Go bindings for [raylib](https://www.raylib.com/), a simple and easy-to-use library to learn videogames programming.
*   [termloop (‚≠ê1.3k)](https://github.com/JoelOtter/termloop) - Terminal-based game engine for Go, built on top of Termbox.
*   [tile (‚≠ê94)](https://github.com/kelindar/tile) - Data-oriented and cache-friendly 2D Grid library (TileMap), includes pathfinding, observers and import/export.

*   [generis (‚≠ê37)](https://github.com/senselogic/GENERIS) - Code generation tool providing generics, free-form macros, conditional compilation and HTML templating.

*   [goverter (‚≠ê213)](https://github.com/jmattheis/goverter) - Generate converters by defining an interface.
*   [GoWrap (‚≠ê722)](https://github.com/hexdigest/gowrap) - Generate decorators for Go interfaces using simple templates.
*   [interfaces (‚≠ê370)](https://github.com/rjeczalik/interfaces) - Command line tool for generating interface definitions.

*   [typeregistry (‚≠ê17)](https://github.com/xiaoxin01/typeregistry) - A library to create type dynamically.

### Goroutines

*   [ants (‚≠ê10k)](https://github.com/panjf2000/ants) - A high-performance and low-cost goroutine pool in Go.
*   [artifex (‚≠ê164)](https://github.com/borderstech/artifex) - Simple in-memory job queue for Golang using worker-based dispatching.
*   [async (‚≠ê107)](https://github.com/reugn/async) - An alternative sync library for Go (Future, Promise, Locks).
*   [async (‚≠ê118)](https://github.com/studiosol/async) - A safe way to execute functions asynchronously, recovering them in case of panic.
*   [breaker (‚≠ê12)](https://github.com/kamilsk/breaker) - Flexible mechanism to make execution flow interruptible.
*   [channelify (‚≠ê27)](https://github.com/ddelizia/channelify) - Transform your function to return channels for easy and powerful parallel processing.
*   [concurrency-limiter (‚≠ê12)](https://github.com/vivek-ng/concurrency-limiter) - Concurrency limiter with support for timeouts , dynamic priority and context cancellation of goroutines.
*   [conexec (‚≠ê13)](https://github.com/ITcathyh/conexec) - A concurrent toolkit to help execute funcs concurrently in an efficient and safe way. It supports specifying the overall timeout to avoid blocking and uses goroutine pool to improve efficiency.
*   [cyclicbarrier (‚≠ê116)](https://github.com/marusama/cyclicbarrier) - CyclicBarrier for golang.
*   [execpool (‚≠ê14)](https://github.com/hexdigest/execpool) - A pool built around exec.Cmd that spins up a given number of processes in advance and attaches stdin and stdout to them when needed. Very similar to FastCGI or Apache Prefork MPM but works for any command.
*   [go-floc (‚≠ê260)](https://github.com/workanator/go-floc) - Orchestrate goroutines with ease.
*   [go-flow (‚≠ê205)](https://github.com/kamildrazkiewicz/go-flow) - Control goroutines execution order.
*   [go-tools/multithreading (‚≠ê11)](https://github.com/nikhilsaraf/go-tools) - Manage a pool of goroutines using this lightweight library with a simple API.
*   [go-trylock (‚≠ê33)](https://github.com/subchen/go-trylock) - TryLock support on read-write lock for Golang.
*   [go-waitgroup (‚≠ê36)](https://github.com/pieterclaerhout/go-waitgroup) - Like `sync.WaitGroup` with error handling and concurrency control.
*   [go-workers (‚≠ê154)](https://github.com/catmullet/go-workers) - Easily and safely run workers for large data processing pipelines.
*   [goccm (‚≠ê62)](https://github.com/zenthangplus/goccm) - Go Concurrency Manager package limits the number of goroutines that allowed to run concurrently.
*   [gohive (‚≠ê44)](https://github.com/loveleshsharma/gohive) - A highly performant and easy to use Goroutine pool for Go.
*   [gollback (‚≠ê106)](https://github.com/vardius/gollback) - asynchronous simple function utilities, for managing execution of closures and callbacks.
*   [gowl (‚≠ê49)](https://github.com/hamed-yousefi/gowl) - Gowl is a process management and process monitoring tool at once. An infinite worker pool gives you the ability to control the pool and processes and monitor their status.
*   [goworker (‚≠ê2.7k)](https://github.com/benmanns/goworker) - goworker is a Go-based background worker.
*   [gowp (‚≠ê438)](https://github.com/xxjwxc/gowp) - gowp is concurrency limiting goroutine pool.
*   [gpool (‚≠ê87)](https://github.com/Sherifabdlnaby/gpool) - manages a resizeable pool of context-aware goroutines to bound concurrency.
*   [grpool (‚≠ê726)](https://github.com/ivpusic/grpool) - Lightweight Goroutine pool.
*   [hands (‚≠ê10)](https://github.com/duanckham/hands) - A process controller used to control the execution and return strategies of multiple goroutines.
*   [Hunch (‚≠ê94)](https://github.com/AaronJan/Hunch) - Hunch provides functions like: `All`, `First`, `Retry`, `Waterfall` etc., that makes asynchronous flow control more intuitive.
*   [kyoo (‚≠ê39)](https://github.com/dirkaholic/kyoo) - Provides an unlimited job queue and concurrent worker pools.
*   [neilotoole/errgroup (‚≠ê144)](https://github.com/neilotoole/errgroup) - Drop-in alternative to `sync/errgroup`, limited to a pool of N worker goroutines.
*   [nursery (‚≠ê58)](https://github.com/arunsworld/nursery) - Structured concurrency in Go.
*   [oversight](https://cirello.io/oversight) - Oversight is a complete implementation of the Erlang supervision trees.
*   [parallel-fn (‚≠ê34)](https://github.com/rafaeljesus/parallel-fn) - Run functions in parallel.
*   [pond (‚≠ê751)](https://github.com/alitto/pond) - Minimalistic and High-performance goroutine worker pool written in Go.
*   [pool (‚≠ê709)](https://github.com/go-playground/pool) - Limited consumer goroutine or unlimited goroutine pool for easier goroutine handling and cancellation.
*   [queue (‚≠ê14)](https://github.com/AnikHasibul/queue) - Gives you a `sync.WaitGroup` like queue group accessibility. Helps you to throttle and limit goroutines, wait for the end of the all goroutines and much more.
*   [routine (‚≠ê56)](https://github.com/x-mod/routine) - go routine control with context, support: Main, Go, Pool and some useful Executors.
*   [semaphore (‚≠ê95)](https://github.com/kamilsk/semaphore) - Semaphore pattern implementation with timeout of lock/unlock operations based on channel and context.
*   [semaphore (‚≠ê160)](https://github.com/marusama/semaphore) - Fast resizable semaphore implementation based on CAS (faster than channel-based semaphore implementations).
*   [stl (‚≠ê26)](https://github.com/ssgreg/stl) - Software transactional locks based on Software Transactional Memory (STM) concurrency control mechanism.
*   [threadpool (‚≠ê86)](https://github.com/shettyh/threadpool) - Golang threadpool implementation.
*   [tunny (‚≠ê3.5k)](https://github.com/Jeffail/tunny) - Goroutine pool for golang.
*   [worker-pool (‚≠ê87)](https://github.com/vardius/worker-pool) - goworker is a Go simple async worker pool.
*   [workerpool (‚≠ê1k)](https://github.com/gammazero/workerpool) - Goroutine pool that limits the concurrency of task execution, not the number of tasks queued.

### Job Scheduler

*   [cheek (‚≠ê72)](https://github.com/datarootsio/cheek) - A simple crontab like scheduler that aims to offer a KISS approach to job scheduling.
*   [clockwerk (‚≠ê133)](https://github.com/onatm/clockwerk) - Go package to schedule periodic jobs using a simple, fluent syntax.
*   [cronticker (‚≠ê8)](https://github.com/krayzpipes/cronticker) - A ticker implementation to support cron schedules.
*   [go-cron (‚≠ê215)](https://github.com/rk/go-cron) - Simple Cron library for go that can execute closures or functions at varying intervals, from once a second to once a year on a specific date and time. Primarily for web applications and long running daemons.
*   [go-quartz (‚≠ê1.1k)](https://github.com/reugn/go-quartz) - Simple, zero-dependency scheduling library for Go.
*   [gocron (‚≠ê2.9k)](https://github.com/go-co-op/gocron) - Easy and fluent Go job scheduling. This is an actively maintained fork of [jasonlvhit/gocron (‚≠ê3.2k)](https://github.com/jasonlvhit/gocron).
*   [gron (‚≠ê950)](https://github.com/roylee0704/gron) - Define time-based tasks using a simple Go API and Gron‚Äôs scheduler will run them accordingly.
*   [gronx (‚≠ê249)](https://github.com/adhocore/gronx) - Cron expression parser, task runner and daemon consuming crontab like task list.
*   [JobRunner (‚≠ê953)](https://github.com/bamzi/jobrunner) - Smart and featureful cron job scheduler with job queuing and live monitoring built in.
*   [jobs (‚≠ê495)](https://github.com/albrow/jobs) - Persistent and flexible background jobs library.
*   [leprechaun (‚≠ê94)](https://github.com/kilgaloon/leprechaun) - Job scheduler that supports webhooks, crons and classic scheduling.
*   [sched (‚≠ê26)](https://github.com/romshark/sched) - A job scheduler with the ability to fast-forward time.
*   [scheduler (‚≠ê417)](https://github.com/carlescere/scheduler) - Cronjobs scheduling made easy.
*   [tasks (‚≠ê143)](https://github.com/madflojo/tasks) - An easy to use in-process scheduler for recurring tasks in Go.

### JSON

*   [ajson (‚≠ê151)](https://github.com/spyzhov/ajson) - Abstract JSON for golang with JSONPath support.
*   [ask (‚≠ê23)](https://github.com/simonnilsson/ask) - Easy access to nested values in maps and slices. Works in combination with encoding/json and other packages that "Unmarshal" arbitrary data into Go data-types.
*   [dynjson (‚≠ê14)](https://github.com/cocoonspace/dynjson) - Client-customizable JSON formats for dynamic APIs.
*   [ej (‚≠ê9)](https://github.com/lucassscaravelli/ej) - Write and read JSON from different sources succinctly.
*   [epoch (‚≠ê11)](https://github.com/vtopc/epoch) - Contains primitives for marshaling/unmarshaling Unix timestamp/epoch to/from build-in time.Time type in JSON.
*   [fastjson (‚≠ê1.8k)](https://github.com/valyala/fastjson) - Fast JSON parser and validator for Go. No custom structs, no code generation, no reflection.
*   [gjo (‚≠ê118)](https://github.com/skanehira/gjo) - Small utility to create JSON objects.
*   [GJSON (‚≠ê12k)](https://github.com/tidwall/gjson) - Get a JSON value with one line of code.
*   [go-jsonerror (‚≠ê13)](https://github.com/ddymko/go-jsonerror) - Go-JsonError is ment to allow us to easily create json response errors that follow the JsonApi spec.
*   [go-respond (‚≠ê51)](https://github.com/nicklaw5/go-respond) - Go package for handling common HTTP JSON responses.
*   [gojq (‚≠ê184)](https://github.com/elgs/gojq) - JSON query in Golang.
*   [gojson (‚≠ê2.6k)](https://github.com/ChimeraCoder/gojson) - Automatically generate Go (golang) struct definitions from example JSON.
*   [JayDiff (‚≠ê95)](https://github.com/yazgazan/jaydiff) - JSON diff utility written in Go.
*   [jettison (‚≠ê141)](https://github.com/wI2L/jettison) - Fast and flexible JSON encoder for Go.
*   [jscan (‚≠ê16)](https://github.com/romshark/jscan) - High performance zero-allocation JSON iterator.
*   [JSON-to-Go](https://mholt.github.io/json-to-go/) - Convert JSON to Go struct.
*   [JSON-to-Proto](https://json-to-proto.github.io/) - Convert JSON to Protobuf online.
*   [json2go (‚≠ê114)](https://github.com/m-zajac/json2go) - Advanced JSON to Go struct conversion. Provides package that can parse multiple JSON documents and create struct to fit them all.
*   [jsonapi-errors (‚≠ê13)](https://github.com/AmuzaTkts/jsonapi-errors) - Go bindings based on the JSON API errors reference.
*   [jsoncolor (‚≠ê28)](https://github.com/neilotoole/jsoncolor) - Drop-in replacement for `encoding/json` that outputs colorized JSON.
*   [jsondiff (‚≠ê225)](https://github.com/wI2L/jsondiff) - JSON diff library for Go based on RFC6902 (JSON Patch).
*   [jsonf (‚≠ê64)](https://github.com/miolini/jsonf) - Console tool for highlighted formatting and struct query fetching JSON.
*   [jsongo (‚≠ê109)](https://github.com/ricardolonga/jsongo) - Fluent API to make it easier to create Json objects.
*   [jsonhal (‚≠ê13)](https://github.com/RichardKnop/jsonhal) - Simple Go package to make custom structs marshal into HAL compatible JSON responses.
*   [jsonic (‚≠ê8)](https://github.com/sinhashubham95/jsonic) - Utilities to handle and query JSON without defining structs in a type safe manner.
*   [jzon (‚≠ê11)](https://github.com/zerosnake0/jzon) - JSON library with standard compatible API/behavior.
*   [kazaam (‚≠ê250)](https://github.com/Qntfy/kazaam) - API for arbitrary transformation of JSON documents.
*   [mapslice-json (‚≠ê15)](https://github.com/mickep76/mapslice-json) - Go MapSlice for ordered marshal/ unmarshal of maps in JSON.
*   [mp (‚≠ê46)](https://github.com/sanbornm/mp) - Simple cli email parser. It currently takes stdin and outputs JSON.
*   [OjG (‚≠ê573)](https://github.com/ohler55/ojg) - Optimized JSON for Go is a high performance parser with a variety of additional JSON tools including JSONPath.
*   [omg.jsonparser (‚≠ê4)](https://github.com/dedalqq/omg.jsonparser) - Simple JSON parser with validation by condition via golang struct fields tags.
*   [ujson (‚≠ê61)](https://github.com/olvrng/ujson) - Fast and minimal JSON parser and transformer that works on unstructured JSON.
*   [vjson (‚≠ê33)](https://github.com/miladibra10/vjson) - Go package for validating JSON objects with declaring a JSON schema with fluent API.

### Logging

*   [distillog (‚≠ê31)](https://github.com/amoghe/distillog) - distilled levelled logging (think of it as stdlib + log levels).
*   [glg (‚≠ê177)](https://github.com/kpango/glg) - glg is simple and fast leveled logging library for Go.
*   [glo (‚≠ê15)](https://github.com/lajosbencz/glo) - PHP Monolog inspired logging facility with identical severity levels.
*   [glog (‚≠ê3.3k)](https://github.com/golang/glog) - Leveled execution logs for Go.
*   [go-cronowriter (‚≠ê54)](https://github.com/utahta/go-cronowriter) - Simple writer that rotate log files automatically based on current date and time, like cronolog.
*   [go-log (‚≠ê13)](https://github.com/subchen/go-log) - Simple and configurable Logging in Go, with level, formatters and writers.
*   [go-log (‚≠ê33)](https://github.com/siddontang/go-log) - Log lib supports level and multi handlers.
*   [go-log (‚≠ê40)](https://github.com/ian-kent/go-log) - Log4j implementation in Go.
*   [go-logger (‚≠ê283)](https://github.com/apsdehal/go-logger) - Simple logger of Go Programs, with level handlers.
*   [gologger (‚≠ê41)](https://github.com/sadlil/gologger) - Simple easy to use log lib for go, logs in Colored Console, Simple Console, File or Elasticsearch.
*   [gomol (‚≠ê19)](https://github.com/aphistic/gomol) - Multiple-output, structured logging for Go with extensible logging outputs.
*   [gone/log (‚≠ê45)](https://github.com/One-com/gone/tree/master/log) - Fast, extendable, full-featured, std-lib source compatible log library.
*   [httpretty (‚≠ê295)](https://github.com/henvic/httpretty) - Pretty-prints your regular HTTP requests on your terminal for debugging (similar to http.DumpRequest).
*   [journald (‚≠ê34)](https://github.com/ssgreg/journald) - Go implementation of systemd Journal's native API for logging.
*   [kemba (‚≠ê9)](https://github.com/clok/kemba) - A tiny debug logging tool inspired by [debug (‚≠ê11k)](https://github.com/visionmedia/debug), great for CLI tools and applications.
*   [log (‚≠ê10)](https://github.com/aerogo/log) - An O(1) logging system that allows you to connect one log to multiple writers (e.g. stdout, a file and a TCP connection).
*   [log (‚≠ê1.3k)](https://github.com/apex/log) - Structured logging package for Go.
*   [log (‚≠ê282)](https://github.com/go-playground/log) - Simple, configurable and scalable Structured Logging for Go.
*   [log (‚≠ê26)](https://github.com/teris-io/log) - Structured log interface for Go cleanly separates logging facade from its implementation.
*   [log-voyage (‚≠ê94)](https://github.com/firstrow/logvoyage) - Full-featured logging saas written in golang.
*   [log15 (‚≠ê1.1k)](https://github.com/inconshreveable/log15) - Simple, powerful logging for Go.
*   [logdump (‚≠ê11)](https://github.com/ewwwwwqm/logdump) - Package for multi-level logging.
*   [logex (‚≠ê40)](https://github.com/chzyer/logex) - Golang log lib, supports tracking and level, wrap by standard log lib.
*   [logger (‚≠ê157)](https://github.com/azer/logger) - Minimalistic logging library for Go.
*   [logmatic (‚≠ê16)](https://github.com/borderstech/logmatic) - Colorized logger for Golang with dynamic log level configuration.
*   [logo (‚≠ê11)](https://github.com/mbndr/logo) - Golang logger to different configurable writers.
*   [logrus (‚≠ê22k)](https://github.com/Sirupsen/logrus) - Structured logger for Go.
*   [logrusiowriter (‚≠ê14)](https://github.com/cabify/logrusiowriter) - `io.Writer` implementation using [logrus (‚≠ê22k)](https://github.com/sirupsen/logrus) logger.
*   [logrusly (‚≠ê28)](https://github.com/sebest/logrusly) - [logrus (‚≠ê22k)](https://github.com/sirupsen/logrus) plug-in to send errors to a [Loggly](https://www.loggly.com/).
*   [logur (‚≠ê188)](https://github.com/logur/logur) - An opinionated logger interface and collection of logging best practices with adapters and integrations for well-known libraries ([logrus (‚≠ê22k)](https://github.com/sirupsen/logrus), [go-kit log (‚≠ê25k)](https://github.com/go-kit/kit/tree/master/log), [zap (‚≠ê18k)](https://github.com/uber-go/zap), [zerolog (‚≠ê7.7k)](https://github.com/rs/zerolog), etc).
*   [logutils (‚≠ê345)](https://github.com/hashicorp/logutils) - Utilities for slightly better logging in Go (Golang) extending the standard logger.
*   [logxi (‚≠ê349)](https://github.com/mgutz/logxi) - 12-factor app logger that is fast and makes you happy.
*   [lumberjack (‚≠ê3.9k)](https://github.com/natefinch/lumberjack) - Simple rolling logger, implements io.WriteCloser.
*   [mlog (‚≠ê30)](https://github.com/jbrodriguez/mlog) - Simple logging module for go, with 5 levels, an optional rotating logfile feature and stdout/stderr output.
*   [noodlog (‚≠ê44)](https://github.com/gyozatech/noodlog) - Parametrized JSON logging library which lets you obfuscate sensitive data and marshal any kind of content. No more printed pointers instead of values, nor escape chars for the JSON strings.
*   [onelog (‚≠ê402)](https://github.com/francoispqt/onelog) - Onelog is a dead simple but very efficient JSON logger. It is the fastest JSON logger out there in all scenarios. Also, it is one of the logger with the lowest allocation.
*   [ozzo-log (‚≠ê121)](https://github.com/go-ozzo/ozzo-log) - High performance logging supporting log severity, categorization, and filtering. Can send filtered log messages to various targets (e.g. console, network, mail).
*   [rollingwriter (‚≠ê258)](https://github.com/arthurkiller/rollingWriter) - RollingWriter is an auto-rotate `io.Writer` implementation with multi policies to provide log file rotation.
*   [seelog (‚≠ê1.6k)](https://github.com/cihub/seelog) - Logging functionality with flexible dispatching, filtering, and formatting.
*   [spew (‚≠ê5.5k)](https://github.com/davecgh/go-spew) - Implements a deep pretty printer for Go data structures to aid in debugging.
*   [stdlog (‚≠ê47)](https://github.com/alexcesaro/log) - Stdlog is an object-oriented library providing leveled logging. It is very useful for cron jobs.
*   [structy/log (‚≠ê5)](https://github.com/structy/log) - A simple to use log system, minimalist but with features for debugging and differentiation of messages.
*   [tail (‚≠ê2.5k)](https://github.com/hpcloud/tail) - Go package striving to emulate the features of the BSD tail program.
*   [xlog (‚≠ê8)](https://github.com/xfxdev/xlog) - Plugin architecture and flexible log system for Go, with level ctrl, multiple log target and custom log format.
*   [xlog (‚≠ê137)](https://github.com/rs/xlog) - Structured logger for `net/context` aware HTTP handlers with flexible dispatching.
*   [yell (‚≠ê1)](https://github.com/jfcg/yell) - Yet another minimalistic logging library.
*   [zap (‚≠ê18k)](https://github.com/uber-go/zap) - Fast, structured, leveled logging in Go.
*   [zerolog (‚≠ê7.7k)](https://github.com/rs/zerolog) - Zero-allocation JSON logger.
*   [zkits-logger (‚≠ê23)](https://github.com/edoger/zkits-logger) - A powerful zero-dependency JSON logger.

### Messaging

*   [ami (‚≠ê26)](https://github.com/kak-tus/ami) - Go client to reliable queues based on Redis Cluster Streams.
*   [amqp (‚≠ê743)](https://github.com/rabbitmq/amqp091-go) - Go RabbitMQ Client Library.
*   [APNs2 (‚≠ê2.8k)](https://github.com/sideshow/apns2) - HTTP/2 Apple Push Notification provider for Go ‚Äî Send push notifications to iOS, tvOS, Safari and OSX apps.
*   [Asynq (‚≠ê5.5k)](https://github.com/hibiken/asynq) - A simple, reliable, and efficient distributed task queue for Go built on top of Redis.
*   [Beaver (‚≠ê1.4k)](https://github.com/Clivern/Beaver) - A real time messaging server to build a scalable in-app notifications, multiplayer games, chat apps in web and mobile apps.
*   [Benthos (‚≠ê5.8k)](https://github.com/Jeffail/benthos) - A message streaming bridge between a range of protocols.
*   [Bus (‚≠ê289)](https://github.com/mustafaturan/bus) - Minimalist message bus implementation for internal communication.
*   [Centrifugo (‚≠ê6.9k)](https://github.com/centrifugal/centrifugo) - Real-time messaging (Websockets or SockJS) server in Go.
*   [Chanify (‚≠ê1k)](https://github.com/chanify/chanify) - A push notification server send message to your iOS devices.
*   [Commander (‚≠ê63)](https://github.com/jeroenrinzema/commander) - A high-level event driven consumer/producer supporting various "dialects" such as Apache Kafka.
*   [Confluent Kafka Golang Client (‚≠ê3.8k)](https://github.com/confluentinc/confluent-kafka-go) - confluent-kafka-go is Confluent's Golang client for Apache Kafka and the Confluent Platform.
*   [dbus (‚≠ê823)](https://github.com/godbus/dbus) - Native Go bindings for D-Bus.
*   [drone-line (‚≠ê78)](https://github.com/appleboy/drone-line) - Sending [Line](https://at.line.me/en) notifications using a binary, docker or Drone CI.
*   [emitter (‚≠ê451)](https://github.com/olebedev/emitter) - Emits events using Go way, with wildcard, predicates, cancellation possibilities and many other good wins.
*   [event (‚≠ê53)](https://github.com/agoalofalife/event) - Implementation of the pattern observer.
*   [EventBus (‚≠ê1.4k)](https://github.com/asaskevich/EventBus) - The lightweight event bus with async compatibility.
*   [gaurun-client (‚≠ê11)](https://github.com/osamingo/gaurun-client) - Gaurun Client written in Go.
*   [Glue (‚≠ê407)](https://github.com/desertbit/glue) - Robust Go and Javascript Socket Library (Alternative to Socket.io).
*   [go-mq (‚≠ê84)](https://github.com/cheshir/go-mq) - RabbitMQ client with declarative configuration.
*   [go-notify (‚≠ê65)](https://github.com/TheCreeper/go-notify) - Native implementation of the freedesktop notification spec.
*   [go-nsq (‚≠ê2.4k)](https://github.com/nsqio/go-nsq) - the official Go package for NSQ.
*   [go-res (‚≠ê62)](https://github.com/jirenius/go-res) - Package for building REST/real-time services where clients are synchronized seamlessly, using NATS and Resgate.
*   [go-socket.io (‚≠ê5k)](https://github.com/googollee/go-socket.io) - socket.io library for golang, a realtime application framework.
*   [go-vitotrol (‚≠ê22)](https://github.com/maxatome/go-vitotrol) - Client library to Viessmann Vitotrol web service.
*   [Gollum (‚≠ê928)](https://github.com/trivago/gollum) - A n:m multiplexer that gathers messages from different sources and broadcasts them to a set of destinations.
*   [golongpoll (‚≠ê623)](https://github.com/jcuga/golongpoll) - HTTP longpoll server library that makes web pub-sub simple.
*   [gopush-cluster (‚≠ê2.1k)](https://github.com/Terry-Mao/gopush-cluster) - gopush-cluster is a go push server cluster.
*   [gorush (‚≠ê6.9k)](https://github.com/appleboy/gorush) - Push notification server using [APNs2 (‚≠ê2.8k)](https://github.com/sideshow/apns2) and google [GCM (‚≠ê103)](https://github.com/google/go-gcm).
*   [gosd (‚≠ê21)](https://github.com/alexsniffin/gosd) - A library for scheduling when to dispatch a message to a channel.
*   [guble (‚≠ê154)](https://github.com/smancke/guble) - Messaging server using push notifications (Google Firebase Cloud Messaging, Apple Push Notification services, SMS) as well as websockets, a REST API, featuring distributed operation and message-persistence.
*   [hare (‚≠ê52)](https://github.com/leozz37/hare) - A user friendly library for sending messages and listening to TCP sockets.
*   [hub (‚≠ê130)](https://github.com/leandro-lugaresi/hub) - A Message/Event Hub for Go applications, using publish/subscribe pattern with support for alias like rabbitMQ exchanges.
*   [jazz (‚≠ê17)](https://github.com/socifi/jazz) - A simple RabbitMQ abstraction layer for queue administration and publishing and consuming of messages.
*   [machinery (‚≠ê6.7k)](https://github.com/RichardKnop/machinery) - Asynchronous task queue/job queue based on distributed message passing.
*   [mangos (‚≠ê572)](https://github.com/nanomsg/mangos) - Pure go implementation of the Nanomsg ("Scalability Protocols") with transport interoperability.
*   [melody (‚≠ê2.9k)](https://github.com/olahol/melody) - Minimalist framework for dealing with websocket sessions, includes broadcasting and automatic ping/pong handling.
*   [Mercure (‚≠ê3.3k)](https://github.com/dunglas/mercure) - Server and library to dispatch server-sent updates using the Mercure protocol (built on top of Server-Sent Events).
*   [messagebus (‚≠ê243)](https://github.com/vardius/message-bus) - messagebus is a Go simple async message bus, perfect for using as event bus when doing event sourcing, CQRS, DDD.
*   [NATS Go Client (‚≠ê4.4k)](https://github.com/nats-io/nats) - Lightweight and high performance publish-subscribe and distributed queueing messaging system - this is the Go library.
*   [nsq-event-bus (‚≠ê75)](https://github.com/rafaeljesus/nsq-event-bus) - A tiny wrapper around NSQ topic and channel.
*   [oplog (‚≠ê114)](https://github.com/dailymotion/oplog) - Generic oplog/replication system for REST APIs.
*   [pubsub (‚≠ê386)](https://github.com/tuxychandru/pubsub) - Simple pubsub package for go.
*   [rabbus (‚≠ê96)](https://github.com/rafaeljesus/rabbus) - A tiny wrapper over amqp exchanges and queues.
*   [rabtap (‚≠ê233)](https://github.com/jandelgado/rabtap) - RabbitMQ swiss army knife cli app.
*   [RapidMQ (‚≠ê65)](https://github.com/sybrexsys/RapidMQ) - RapidMQ is a lightweight and reliable library for managing of the local messages queue.
*   [redisqueue (‚≠ê106)](https://github.com/robinjoseph08/redisqueue) - redisqueue provides a producer and consumer of a queue that uses Redis streams.
*   [rmqconn (‚≠ê20)](https://github.com/sbabiv/rmqconn) - RabbitMQ Reconnection. Wrapper over amqp.Connection and amqp.Dial. Allowing to do a reconnection when the connection is broken before forcing the call to the Close () method to be closed.
*   [sarama (‚≠ê9.7k)](https://github.com/Shopify/sarama) - Go library for Apache Kafka.
*   [Uniqush-Push (‚≠ê1.5k)](https://github.com/uniqush/uniqush-push) - Redis backed unified push service for server-side notifications to mobile devices.
*   [zmq4 (‚≠ê1k)](https://github.com/pebbe/zmq4) - Go interface to ZeroMQ version 4. Also available for [version 3 (‚≠ê133)](https://github.com/pebbe/zmq3) and [version 2 (‚≠ê18)](https://github.com/pebbe/zmq2).

### Dependency Injection

*   [alice (‚≠ê51)](https://github.com/magic003/alice) - Additive dependency injection container for Golang.
*   [di (‚≠ê175)](https://github.com/goava/di) - A dependency injection container for go programming language.
*   [dig (‚≠ê3k)](https://github.com/uber-go/dig) - A reflection based dependency injection toolkit for Go.
*   [dingo (‚≠ê160)](https://github.com/i-love-flamingo/dingo) - A dependency injection toolkit for Go, based on Guice.
*   [fx (‚≠ê3.7k)](https://github.com/uber-go/fx) - A dependency injection based application framework for Go (built on top of dig).
*   [gocontainer (‚≠ê18)](https://github.com/vardius/gocontainer) - Simple Dependency Injection Container.
*   [goioc/di (‚≠ê246)](https://github.com/goioc/di) - Spring-inspired Dependency Injection Container.
*   [google/wire (‚≠ê10k)](https://github.com/google/wire) - Automated Initialization in Go.
*   [HnH/di (‚≠ê6)](https://github.com/HnH/di) - DI container library that is focused on clean API and flexibility.
*   [kinit (‚≠ê9)](https://github.com/go-kata/kinit) - Customizable dependency injection container with the global mode, cascade initialization and panic-safe finalization.
*   [linker (‚≠ê36)](https://github.com/logrange/linker) - A reflection based dependency injection and inversion of control library with components lifecycle support.
*   [wire (‚≠ê38)](https://github.com/Fs02/wire) - Strict Runtime Dependency Injection for Golang.

### Project Layout

*   [ardanlabs/service (‚≠ê2.6k)](https://github.com/ardanlabs/service) - A [starter kit (‚≠ê2.6k)](https://github.com/ardanlabs/service/wiki) for building production grade scalable web service applications.
*   [cookiecutter-golang (‚≠ê582)](https://github.com/lacion/cookiecutter-golang) - A Go application boilerplate template for quick starting projects following production best practices.
*   [go-sample (‚≠ê117)](https://github.com/zitryss/go-sample) - A sample layout for Go application projects with the real code.
*   [go-starter (‚≠ê309)](https://github.com/allaboutapps/go-starter) - An opinionated production-ready RESTful JSON backend template, highly integrated with VSCode DevContainers.
*   [go-todo-backend (‚≠ê204)](https://github.com/Fs02/go-todo-backend) - Go Todo Backend example using modular project layout for product microservice.
*   [gobase (‚≠ê45)](https://github.com/wajox/gobase) - A simple skeleton for golang application with basic setup for real golang application.
*   [golang-standards/project-layout (‚≠ê38k)](https://github.com/golang-standards/project-layout) - Set of common historical and emerging project layout patterns in the Go ecosystem. Note: despite the org-name they do not represent official golang standards, see [this issue (‚≠ê38k)](https://github.com/golang-standards/project-layout/issues/117) for more information. Nonetheless, some may find the layout useful.
*   [golang-templates/seed (‚≠ê368)](https://github.com/golang-templates/seed) - Go application GitHub repository template.
*   [insidieux/inizio (‚≠ê14)](https://github.com/insidieux/inizio) - Golang project layout generator with plugins.
*   [modern-go-application (‚≠ê1.5k)](https://github.com/sagikazarmark/modern-go-application) - Go application boilerplate and example applying modern practices.
*   [scaffold (‚≠ê136)](https://github.com/catchplay/scaffold) - Scaffold generates a starter Go project layout. Lets you focus on business logic implemented.
*   [wangyoucao577/go-project-layout (‚≠ê19)](https://github.com/wangyoucao577/go-project-layout) - Set of practices and discussions on how to structure Go project layout.

### Strings

*   [bexp (‚≠ê0)](https://github.com/mkungla/bexp) - Go implementation of Brace Expansion mechanism to generate arbitrary strings.

### Morphological Analyzers

*   [go-stem (‚≠ê74)](https://github.com/agonopol/go-stem) - Implementation of the porter stemming algorithm.
*   [go2vec (‚≠ê50)](https://github.com/danieldk/go2vec) - Reader and utility functions for word2vec embeddings.
*   [golibstemmer (‚≠ê20)](https://github.com/rjohnsondev/golibstemmer) - Go bindings for the snowball libstemmer library including porter 2.
*   [gosentiwordnet (‚≠ê10)](https://github.com/dinopuguh/gosentiwordnet) - Sentiment analyzer using sentiwordnet lexicon in Go.
*   [govader (‚≠ê29)](https://github.com/jonreiter/govader) - Go implementation of [VADER Sentiment Analysis (‚≠ê3.9k)](https://github.com/cjhutto/vaderSentiment).
*   [kagome (‚≠ê709)](https://github.com/ikawaha/kagome) - JP morphological analyzer written in pure Go.
*   [libtextcat (‚≠ê12)](https://github.com/goodsign/libtextcat) - Cgo binding for libtextcat C library. Guaranteed compatibility with version 2.2.
*   [nlp (‚≠ê379)](https://github.com/Shixzie/nlp) - Extract values from strings and fill your structs with nlp.
*   [nlp (‚≠ê392)](https://github.com/james-bowman/nlp) - Go Natural Language Processing library supporting LSA (Latent Semantic Analysis).
*   [paicehusk (‚≠ê29)](https://github.com/rookii/paicehusk) - Golang implementation of the Paice/Husk Stemming Algorithm.
*   [porter (‚≠ê12)](https://github.com/a2800276/porter) - This is a fairly straightforward port of Martin Porter's C implementation of the Porter stemming algorithm.
*   [porter2 (‚≠ê46)](https://github.com/zhenjl/porter2) - Really fast Porter 2 stemmer.
*   [RAKE.go (‚≠ê97)](https://github.com/afjoseph/RAKE.Go) - Go port of the Rapid Automatic Keyword Extraction Algorithm (RAKE).

### Networking

*   [arp (‚≠ê307)](https://github.com/mdlayher/arp) - Package arp implements the ARP protocol, as described in RFC 826.
*   [buffstreams (‚≠ê252)](https://github.com/stabbycutyou/buffstreams) - Streaming protocolbuffer data over TCP made easy.
*   [canopus (‚≠ê150)](https://github.com/zubairhamed/canopus) - CoAP Client/Server implementation (RFC 7252).
*   [cidranger (‚≠ê811)](https://github.com/yl2chen/cidranger) - Fast IP to CIDR lookup for Go.
*   [dhcp6 (‚≠ê76)](https://github.com/mdlayher/dhcp6) - Package dhcp6 implements a DHCPv6 server, as described in RFC 3315.
*   [dns (‚≠ê6.8k)](https://github.com/miekg/dns) - Go library for working with DNS.
*   [dnsmonster (‚≠ê246)](https://github.com/mosajjal/dnsmonster) - Passive DNS Capture/Monitoring Framework.
*   [easytcp (‚≠ê591)](https://github.com/DarthPestilane/easytcp) - A light-weight TCP framework written in Go (Golang), built with message router. EasyTCP helps you build a TCP server easily fast and less painful.
*   [ether (‚≠ê78)](https://github.com/songgao/ether) - Cross-platform Go package for sending and receiving ethernet frames.
*   [ethernet (‚≠ê255)](https://github.com/mdlayher/ethernet) - Package ethernet implements marshaling and unmarshaling of IEEE 802.3 Ethernet II frames and IEEE 802.1Q VLAN tags.
*   [fasthttp (‚≠ê19k)](https://github.com/valyala/fasthttp) - Package fasthttp is a fast HTTP implementation for Go, up to 10 times faster than net/http.
*   [fortio (‚≠ê2.8k)](https://github.com/fortio/fortio) - Load testing library and command line tool, advanced echo server and web UI. Allows to specify a set query-per-second load and record latency histograms and other useful stats and graph them. Tcp, Http, gRPC.
*   [ftp (‚≠ê1.1k)](https://github.com/jlaffaye/ftp) - Package ftp implements a FTP client as described in [RFC 959](https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc959).
*   [ftpserverlib (‚≠ê346)](https://github.com/fclairamb/ftpserverlib) - Fully featured FTP server library.
*   [gaio (‚≠ê482)](https://github.com/xtaci/gaio) - High performance async-io networking for Golang in proactor mode.
*   [gev (‚≠ê1.6k)](https://github.com/Allenxuxu/gev) - gev is a lightweight, fast non-blocking TCP network library based on Reactor mode.
*   [gmqtt (‚≠ê842)](https://github.com/DrmagicE/gmqtt) - Gmqtt is a flexible, high-performance MQTT broker library that fully implements the MQTT protocol V3.1.1.
*   [gnet (‚≠ê7.4k)](https://github.com/panjf2000/gnet) - `gnet` is a high-performance, lightweight, non-blocking, event-driven networking framework written in pure Go.
*   [gNxI (‚≠ê228)](https://github.com/google/gnxi) - A collection of tools for Network Management that use the gNMI and gNOI protocols.
*   [go-getter (‚≠ê1.5k)](https://github.com/hashicorp/go-getter) - Go library for downloading files or directories from various sources using a URL.
*   [go-powerdns (‚≠ê71)](https://github.com/joeig/go-powerdns) - PowerDNS API bindings for Golang.
*   [go-stun (‚≠ê557)](https://github.com/ccding/go-stun) - Go implementation of the STUN client (RFC 3489 and RFC 5389).
*   [gobgp (‚≠ê3.2k)](https://github.com/osrg/gobgp) - BGP implemented in the Go Programming Language.
*   [golibwireshark (‚≠ê28)](https://github.com/sunwxg/golibwireshark) - Package golibwireshark use libwireshark library to decode pcap file and analyse dissection data.
*   [gopacket (‚≠ê5.5k)](https://github.com/google/gopacket) - Go library for packet processing with libpcap bindings.
*   [gopcap (‚≠ê466)](https://github.com/akrennmair/gopcap) - Go wrapper for libpcap.
*   [goshark (‚≠ê16)](https://github.com/sunwxg/goshark) - Package goshark use tshark to decode IP packet and create data struct to analyse packet.
*   [gosnmp (‚≠ê947)](https://github.com/soniah/gosnmp) - Native Go library for performing SNMP actions.
*   [gotcp (‚≠ê506)](https://github.com/gansidui/gotcp) - Go package for quickly writing tcp applications.
*   [grab (‚≠ê1.2k)](https://github.com/cavaliercoder/grab) - Go package for managing file downloads.
*   [graval (‚≠ê28)](https://github.com/koofr/graval) - Experimental FTP server framework.
*   [HTTPLab (‚≠ê3.9k)](https://github.com/gchaincl/httplab) - HTTPLabs let you inspect HTTP requests and forge responses.
*   [httpproxy (‚≠ê19)](https://github.com/wzshiming/httpproxy) - HTTP proxy handler and dialer.
*   [iplib (‚≠ê106)](https://github.com/c-robinson/iplib) - Library for working with IP addresses (net.IP, net.IPNet), inspired by python [ipaddress](https://docs.python.org/3/library/ipaddress.html) and ruby [ipaddr](https://ruby-doc.org/stdlib-2.5.1/libdoc/ipaddr/rdoc/IPAddr.html)
*   [jazigo (‚≠ê189)](https://github.com/udhos/jazigo) - Jazigo is a tool written in Go for retrieving configuration for multiple network devices.
*   [kcp-go (‚≠ê3.6k)](https://github.com/xtaci/kcp-go) - KCP - Fast and Reliable ARQ Protocol.
*   [kcptun (‚≠ê13k)](https://github.com/xtaci/kcptun) - Extremely simple & fast udp tunnel based on KCP protocol.
*   [lhttp (‚≠ê682)](https://github.com/fanux/lhttp) - Powerful websocket framework, build your IM server more easily.
*   [linkio (‚≠ê53)](https://github.com/ian-kent/linkio) - Network link speed simulation for Reader/Writer interfaces.
*   [llb (‚≠ê14)](https://github.com/kirillDanshin/llb) - It's a very simple but quick backend for proxy servers. Can be useful for fast redirection to predefined domain with zero memory allocation and fast response.
*   [mdns (‚≠ê952)](https://github.com/hashicorp/mdns) - Simple mDNS (Multicast DNS) client/server library in Golang.
*   [mqttPaho](https://eclipse.org/paho/clients/golang/) - The Paho Go Client provides an MQTT client library for connection to MQTT brokers via TCP, TLS or WebSockets.
*   [nbio (‚≠ê1.3k)](https://github.com/lesismal/nbio) - Pure Go 1000k+ connections solution, support tls/http1.x/websocket and basically compatible with net/http, with high-performance and low memory cost, non-blocking, event-driven, easy-to-use.
*   [netpoll (‚≠ê3.4k)](https://github.com/cloudwego/netpoll) - A high-performance non-blocking I/O networking framework, which focused on RPC scenarios, developed by ByteDance.
*   [NFF-Go (‚≠ê1.3k)](https://github.com/intel-go/nff-go) - Framework for rapid development of performant network functions for cloud and bare-metal (former YANFF).
*   [packet (‚≠ê71)](https://github.com/aerogo/packet) - Send packets over TCP and UDP. It can buffer messages and hot-swap connections if needed.
*   [panoptes-stream (‚≠ê39)](https://github.com/yahoo/panoptes-stream) - A cloud native distributed streaming network telemetry (gNMI, Juniper JTI and Cisco MDT).
*   [peerdiscovery (‚≠ê583)](https://github.com/schollz/peerdiscovery) - Pure Go library for cross-platform local peer discovery using UDP multicast.
*   [portproxy (‚≠ê52)](https://github.com/aybabtme/portproxy) - Simple TCP proxy which adds CORS support to API's which don't support it.
*   [publicip (‚≠ê26)](https://github.com/polera/publicip) - Package publicip returns your public facing IPv4 address (internet egress).
*   [quic-go (‚≠ê7.9k)](https://github.com/lucas-clemente/quic-go) - An implementation of the QUIC protocol in pure Go.
*   [raw (‚≠ê423)](https://github.com/mdlayher/raw) - Package raw enables reading and writing data at the device driver level for a network interface.
*   [sftp (‚≠ê1.3k)](https://github.com/pkg/sftp) - Package sftp implements the SSH File Transfer Protocol as described in <https://filezilla-project.org/specs/draft-ietf-secsh-filexfer-02.txt>.
*   [ssh (‚≠ê2.9k)](https://github.com/gliderlabs/ssh) - Higher-level API for building SSH servers (wraps crypto/ssh).
*   [sslb (‚≠ê145)](https://github.com/eduardonunesp/sslb) - It's a Super Simples Load Balancer, just a little project to achieve some kind of performance.
*   [stun (‚≠ê488)](https://github.com/go-rtc/stun) - Go implementation of RFC 5389 STUN protocol.
*   [tcp\_server (‚≠ê419)](https://github.com/firstrow/tcp_server) - Go library for building tcp servers faster.
*   [tspool (‚≠ê14)](https://github.com/two/tspool) - A TCP Library use worker pool to improve performance and protect your server.
*   [utp (‚≠ê166)](https://github.com/anacrolix/utp) - Go uTP micro transport protocol implementation.
*   [vssh (‚≠ê886)](https://github.com/yahoo/vssh) - Go library for building network and server automation over SSH protocol.
*   [water (‚≠ê1.6k)](https://github.com/songgao/water) - Simple TUN/TAP library.
*   [webrtc (‚≠ê11k)](https://github.com/pions/webrtc) - A pure Go implementation of the WebRTC API.
*   [winrm (‚≠ê395)](https://github.com/masterzen/winrm) - Go WinRM client to remotely execute commands on Windows machines.
*   [xtcp (‚≠ê140)](https://github.com/xfxdev/xtcp) - TCP Server Framework with simultaneous full duplex communication, graceful shutdown, and custom protocol.

### HTTP Clients

*   [gentleman (‚≠ê998)](https://github.com/h2non/gentleman) - Full-featured plugin-driven HTTP client library.
*   [go-http-client (‚≠ê51)](https://github.com/bozd4g/go-http-client) - Make http calls simply and easily.
*   [go-req (‚≠ê19)](https://github.com/wenerme/go-req) - Declarative golang HTTP client.
*   [go-retryablehttp (‚≠ê1.5k)](https://github.com/hashicorp/go-retryablehttp) - Retryable HTTP client in Go.
*   [grequests (‚≠ê1.9k)](https://github.com/levigross/grequests) - A Go "clone" of the great and famous Requests library.
*   [heimdall (‚≠ê2.4k)](https://github.com/gojektech/heimdall) - An enhanced http client with retry and hystrix capabilities.
*   [httpretry (‚≠ê29)](https://github.com/ybbus/httpretry) - Enriches the default go HTTP client with retry functionality.
*   [pester (‚≠ê615)](https://github.com/sethgrid/pester) - Go HTTP client calls with retries, backoff, and concurrency.
*   [request (‚≠ê228)](https://github.com/monaco-io/request) - HTTP client for golang. If you have experience about axios or requests, you will love it. No 3rd dependency.
*   [requests (‚≠ê555)](https://github.com/carlmjohnson/requests) - HTTP requests for Gophers. Uses context.Context and doesn't hide the underlying net/http.Client, making it compatible with standard Go APIs. Also includes testing tools.
*   [resty (‚≠ê7.4k)](https://github.com/go-resty/resty) - Simple HTTP and REST client for Go inspired by Ruby rest-client.
*   [rq (‚≠ê45)](https://github.com/ddo/rq) - A nicer interface for golang stdlib HTTP client.
*   [sling (‚≠ê1.5k)](https://github.com/dghubble/sling) - Sling is a Go HTTP client library for creating and sending API requests.

### OpenGL

*   [gl (‚≠ê951)](https://github.com/go-gl/gl) - Go bindings for OpenGL (generated via glow).
*   [glfw (‚≠ê1.4k)](https://github.com/go-gl/glfw) - Go bindings for GLFW 3.
*   [go-glmatrix (‚≠ê7)](https://github.com/technohippy/go-glmatrix) - Go port of [glMatrix](https://glmatrix.net/) library.
*   [goxjs/gl (‚≠ê162)](https://github.com/goxjs/gl) - Go cross-platform OpenGL bindings (OS X, Linux, Windows, browsers, iOS, Android).
*   [goxjs/glfw (‚≠ê76)](https://github.com/goxjs/glfw) - Go cross-platform glfw library for creating an OpenGL context and receiving events.
*   [mathgl (‚≠ê475)](https://github.com/go-gl/mathgl) - Pure Go math package specialized for 3D math, with inspiration from GLM.

### ORM

*   [cacheme (‚≠ê22)](https://github.com/Yiling-J/cacheme-go) - Schema based, typed Redis caching/memoize framework for Go.
*   [ent (‚≠ê13k)](https://github.com/facebook/ent) - An entity framework for Go. Simple, yet powerful ORM for modeling and querying data.
*   [go-firestorm (‚≠ê40)](https://github.com/jschoedt/go-firestorm) - A simple ORM for Google/Firebase Cloud Firestore.
*   [go-sql (‚≠ê170)](https://github.com/rushteam/gosql) - A easy ORM for mysql.
*   [go-sqlbuilder (‚≠ê952)](https://github.com/huandu/go-sqlbuilder) - A flexible and powerful SQL string builder library plus a zero-config ORM.
*   [go-store (‚≠ê109)](https://github.com/gosuri/go-store) - Simple and fast Redis backed key-value store library for Go.
*   [GORM (‚≠ê32k)](https://github.com/go-gorm/gorm) - The fantastic ORM library for Golang, aims to be developer friendly.
*   [gormt (‚≠ê2.1k)](https://github.com/xxjwxc/gormt) - Mysql database to golang gorm struct.
*   [gorp (‚≠ê3.6k)](https://github.com/go-gorp/gorp) - Go Relational Persistence, ORM-ish library for Go.
*   [grimoire (‚≠ê159)](https://github.com/Fs02/grimoire) - Grimoire is a database access layer and validation for golang. (Support: MySQL, PostgreSQL and SQLite3).
*   [lore (‚≠ê11)](https://github.com/abrahambotros/lore) - Simple and lightweight pseudo-ORM/pseudo-struct-mapping environment for Go.
*   [marlow (‚≠ê13)](https://github.com/marlow/marlow) - Generated ORM from project structs for compile time safety assurances.
*   [pop/soda (‚≠ê1.3k)](https://github.com/gobuffalo/pop) - Database migration, creation, ORM, etc... for MySQL, PostgreSQL, and SQLite.
*   [Prisma (‚≠ê1.4k)](https://github.com/prisma/prisma-client-go) - Prisma Client Go, Typesafe database access for Go.
*   [reform (‚≠ê1.4k)](https://github.com/go-reform/reform) - Better ORM for Go, based on non-empty interfaces and code generation.
*   [rel (‚≠ê628)](https://github.com/go-rel/rel) - Modern Database Access Layer for Golang - Testable, Extendable and Crafted Into a Clean and Elegant API.
*   [SQLBoiler (‚≠ê5.6k)](https://github.com/volatiletech/sqlboiler) - ORM generator. Generate a featureful and blazing-fast ORM tailored to your database schema.
*   [upper.io/db (‚≠ê3.3k)](https://github.com/upper/db) - Single interface for interacting with different data sources through the use of adapters that wrap mature database drivers.
*   [XORM](https://gitea.com/xorm/xorm) - Simple and powerful ORM for Go. (Support: MySQL, MyMysql, PostgreSQL, Tidb, SQLite3, MsSql and Oracle).
*   [Zoom (‚≠ê297)](https://github.com/albrow/zoom) - Blazing-fast datastore and querying engine built on Redis.

### Package Management

*   [go modules](https://golang.org/cmd/go/#hdr-Modules__module_versions__and_more) - Modules are the unit of source code interchange and versioning. The go command has direct support for working with modules, including recording and resolving dependencies on other modules.
*   [dep (‚≠ê13k)](https://github.com/golang/dep) - Go dependency tool.
*   [vgo](https://go.googlesource.com/vgo/) - Versioned Go.
*   [glide (‚≠ê8.2k)](https://github.com/Masterminds/glide) - Manage your golang vendor and vendored packages with ease. Inspired by tools like Maven, Bundler, and Pip.
*   [godep (‚≠ê5.6k)](https://github.com/tools/godep) - dependency tool for go, godep helps build packages reproducibly by fixing their dependencies.
*   [gom (‚≠ê1.4k)](https://github.com/mattn/gom) - Go Manager - bundle for go.
*   [goop (‚≠ê779)](https://github.com/nitrous-io/goop) - Simple dependency manager for Go (golang), inspired by Bundler.
*   [gop (‚≠ê50)](https://github.com/lunny/gop) - Build and manage your Go applications out of GOPATH.
*   [gopm (‚≠ê2.5k)](https://github.com/gpmgo/gopm) - Go Package Manager.
*   [govendor (‚≠ê5k)](https://github.com/kardianos/govendor) - Go Package Manager. Go vendor tool that works with the standard vendor file.
*   [gpm (‚≠ê1.2k)](https://github.com/pote/gpm) - Barebones dependency manager for Go.
*   [johnny-deps (‚≠ê214)](https://github.com/VividCortex/johnny-deps) - Minimal dependency version using Git.
*   [modgv (‚≠ê445)](https://github.com/lucasepe/modgv) - Converts 'go mod graph' output into Graphviz's DOT language.
*   [mvn-golang (‚≠ê151)](https://github.com/raydac/mvn-golang) - plugin that provides way for auto-loading of Golang SDK, dependency management and start build environment in Maven project infrastructure.
*   [nut (‚≠ê238)](https://github.com/jingweno/nut) - Vendor Go dependencies.
*   [VenGO (‚≠ê124)](https://github.com/DamnWidget/VenGO) - create and manage exportable isolated go virtual environments.

*   [gojsonq (‚≠ê2k)](https://github.com/thedevsaddam/gojsonq) - A simple Go package to Query over JSON Data.

*   [straf (‚≠ê34)](https://github.com/SonicRoshan/straf) - Easily Convert Golang structs to GraphQL objects.

### Resource Embedding

*   [debme (‚≠ê22)](https://github.com/leaanthony/debme) - Create an `embed.FS` from an existing `embed.FS` subdirectory.
*   [esc (‚≠ê632)](https://github.com/mjibson/esc) - Embeds files into Go programs and provides http.FileSystem interfaces to them.
